2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a><figcaption>House with blue tarp after Hurricane Maria in Dorado, Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In mid 2018, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">United States Army Corps of Engineers</a> announced it would be undertaking a major <a href="/wiki/Flood_control" title="Flood control">flood control</a> project of a river that often causes flooding in Dorado, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado de la Plata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_USACE_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_USACE-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Act_60">Act 60</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Act 60"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Fortu%C3%B1o" title="Luis Fortu\xc3\xb1o">Luis Fortu\xc3\xb1o</a> administration passes broad tax incentives for foreigners through Acts 20 and 22 (later consolidated into Act 60\xe2\x80\x932019), which included 0% on capital gains and a 4% corporate rate. Some areas became favored by the individuals that arrived to Puerto Rico to benefit, including Dorado Beach where mansions and villas sold in the 20\xe2\x80\x9330&#160;million range.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The price of property in Dorado rose 66% between 2016 and 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the turn of the decade more foreigners have moved to Dorado Beach, including Kevin Thobias and <a href="/wiki/Logan_Paul" title="Logan Paul">Logan Paul</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio-Plata-Dorado-PR.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rio-Plata-Dorado-PR.jpg/250px-Rio-Plata-Dorado-PR.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rio-Plata-Dorado-PR.jpg/375px-Rio-Plata-Dorado-PR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rio-Plata-Dorado-PR.jpg/500px-Rio-Plata-Dorado-PR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>La Plata River in 2007</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Dorado is located in Puerto Rico\'s <a href="/wiki/Northern_Karst_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Karst (Puerto Rico)">Northern Karst</a> region. Much of its geology consists of alluvial and coastal/estuarine sediments of <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> age and <a href="/wiki/Limestones" class="mw-redirect" title="Limestones">limestones</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tertiary" title="Tertiary">Tertiary</a> age.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The limestones are mostly in the south part of the municipality, in <a href="/wiki/Espinosa,_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Espinosa, Dorado, Puerto Rico">Espinosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maguayo" title="Maguayo">Maguayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Lajas,_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Lajas, Dorado, Puerto Rico">Rio Lajas</a> barrios. These limestones exhibit mature <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> topography of great beauty. It has been subjected to extensive <a href="/wiki/Quarrying" class="mw-redirect" title="Quarrying">quarrying</a>, which have left unsightly scars in the landscape. Some local communities have gathered efforts to minimize quarrying and improve land management to protect the remaining karst topography and the fauna and flora that lives in it. Around 95% of Dorado\'s terrain are flood plains while the rest is part of a limestone region.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino103_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino103-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The terrains are naturally fertilized when the Dorado, Plata and Lajas rivers go out of their limits.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino103_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino103-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The rock formation known as Ojo de Buey is tourist attraction, also being associated with legends of ghosts and the claim that the pirate captain <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Cofres%C3%AD" title="Roberto Cofres\xc3\xad">Roberto Cofres\xc3\xad</a>\'s treasure is buried near it.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino334_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino334-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hydrography">Hydrography</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hydrography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Some of the rivers of Dorado are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Rivers: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Cocal" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Cocal">R\xc3\xado Cocal</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Lajas" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Lajas">R\xc3\xado Lajas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado de la Plata</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Nuevo" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Nuevo">R\xc3\xado Nuevo</a>.</li>\n<li>Mata Redonda Lagoon<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Punta Fraile marsh<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dorado,_PuertoRico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Dorado%2C_PuertoRico_locator_map.png/220px-Dorado%2C_PuertoRico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Dorado%2C_PuertoRico_locator_map.png/330px-Dorado%2C_PuertoRico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Dorado%2C_PuertoRico_locator_map.png/440px-Dorado%2C_PuertoRico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1191" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Dorado.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Dorado is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Dorado_barrio-pueblo" title="Dorado barrio-pueblo">Dorado barrio-pueblo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Espinosa,_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Espinosa, Dorado, Puerto Rico">Espinosa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Higuillar" title="Higuillar">Higuillar</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maguayo" title="Maguayo">Maguayo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mameyal" title="Mameyal">Mameyal</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Lajas,_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Lajas, Dorado, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Lajas</a></li></ol>\n<p>Some of the municipality\'s barrios are named after the name of its inhabitants or ta\xc3\xadno names, even the region itself may have been taken from the last name of an early Spanish settler.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino210_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino210-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Examples of this are Espinosa and Maguayo<sup id="cite_ref-Canino211_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino211-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Others such as Higuilar, Mameyal, Marismillas and R\xc3\xado Lajas are named after flora or geographical features.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino212_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino212-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_barrios_and_sectors_of_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of barrios and sectors of Dorado, Puerto Rico">List of barrios and sectors of Dorado, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are like <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-sectors_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sectors-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Dorado: El Ca\xc3\xb1o, Kuilan Barrio Espinosa, La Hormiga, Sector Calondrias, Sector El Cotto, Villa 2000, Villa Iriarte, and Villa Plata.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Dorado has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> that is very hot in the summer months and warm in the winter. Temperatures range around 60 to 80&#160;\xc2\xb0F (16 to 27&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in the winter and 75 to 95&#160;\xc2\xb0F (24 to 35&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in the summer.\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium" class="notheme">56.68<br />(1,439)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: <a href="/wiki/The_Weather_Channel" title="The Weather Channel">The Weather Channel</a><sup id="cite_ref-TWC_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TWC-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tourism">Tourism</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign, with a passport book and website. The Dorado page lists <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Sala de exposiciones del plata Salvador Rivera Cardona</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Plaza Conmemorativa 5th Centenario</i></span>, and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Balneario Manuel "Nolo" Morales</i></span>, as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Beach_in_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4577" data-file-height="3027" /></a><figcaption>A rocky beach in Dorado</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Dorado\'s cultural activities feature all of the traditional Puerto Rican elements, but focus on African and Spanish elements.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino145_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino145-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ta\xc3\xadno elements are more conspicuous and mostly influence the food.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino145_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino145-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Popular culture is promoted, which is represented by a number of interpreters such as Juan Boria, Joe Valle and Horacio Olivo.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino146_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino146-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Local painters include Jos\xc3\xa9 Bernandino and Marcos J. Alegr\xc3\xada.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino146_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino146-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the early 20th century the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_family" title="Rockefeller family">Rockefeller family</a> purchased plots of land in the northwest region of the municipality of Dorado where they built a huge private vacation compound. <a href="/wiki/Laurance_Rockefeller" title="Laurance Rockefeller">Laurance Rockefeller</a> would later use this land to create Dorado Beach Hotel and Golf Club, which later became the Dorado Beach <a href="/wiki/Hyatt" title="Hyatt">Hyatt</a> Hotel which closed in 2007. Dorado Beach Hotel became a <a href="/wiki/The_Ritz-Carlton_Hotel_Company" title="The Ritz-Carlton Hotel Company">Ritz Carlton</a> hotel in 2012, which got the top spot in the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9_Nast" title="Cond\xc3\xa9 Nast">Conde Naste</a> Readers\' Choice.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorado has long been known as a golf haven. Its tourist industry includes the Dorado Beach Resort (Ritz-Carlton Reserve &amp; Plantation), the Hyatt Hacienda del Mar, and Embassy Suites in the Dorado Del Mar neighborhood. As of 2014 there are three operating golf courses in the municipality, the Dorado Beach East Course, the Plantation Sugarcane Course and the Plantation Pineapple Course. The Dorado del Mar course closed in 2014.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Beach_chairs_on_a_beach_in_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Beach_chairs_on_a_beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Beach_chairs_on_a_beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Beach_chairs_on_a_beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Beach_chairs_on_a_beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Beach_chairs_on_a_beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Beach_chairs_on_a_beach_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4084" data-file-height="2723" /></a><figcaption>Beach chairs on a beach in Dorado</figcaption></figure>\n<p>According to a news article by <a href="/wiki/Primera_Hora_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Primera Hora (Puerto Rico)">Primera Hora</a>, Dorado has 24 beaches, including <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Balneario Manuel Nolo Morales</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the places to visit in Dorado are located <a href="/wiki/Dorado_barrio-pueblo" title="Dorado barrio-pueblo">downtown</a>. For example, the Museum <a href="/wiki/Casa_del_Rey" title="Casa del Rey">Casa del Rey</a> is the house built in most towns controlled by Spain during their colonization, which was intended for the King and <a href="/wiki/Queen_consort" title="Queen consort">Queen</a> to stay if they visited. The museum includes several artifacts from the era. There\'s also the Distinguished Dorade\xc3\xb1os Square, and the <a href="/wiki/Juan_Boria" title="Juan Boria">Juan Boria</a> Theater. The last one was recently reopened after a long period of restoration.\n</p><p>Some of the most visited beaches in Dorado are Sardinera, Kikita and El Unico are other beaches frequented by <a href="/wiki/Surfers" class="mw-redirect" title="Surfers">surfers</a>. The Ojo del Buey Park is a park located at the <a href="/wiki/Base_level" title="Base level">base level</a> of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">La Plata River</a>. The name comes from a rock formation that has the shape of an <a href="/wiki/Ox" title="Ox">ox</a>. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado_Pterocarpus_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dorado Pterocarpus Forest (page does not exist)">Dorado Pterocarpus Forest</a> is also located in the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorado also has a church called the Sanctuary of Christ of the Reconciliation, that has the third largest statue of <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ">Jesus Christ</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, inside its temple. Christmas celebrations extend throughout the season and into epiphany, prior to them the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Strenna_Mass&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Strenna Mass (page does not exist)">Strenna Mass</a> is held and on Christmas Eve, the <a href="/wiki/Misa_de_Gallo" title="Misa de Gallo">Misa de Gallo</a> takes place.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino169_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino169-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Folk traditions tied to these events include the sprinkling of sugar in houses to receive the new year, a practice where a man dresses as a representation of the old year with which residents have fun or release their frustrations for the fading year and trulla parties in which people dressed as the Three Wise Men and a vigil where music is played to celebrate the epiphany.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino173_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino173-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As in the rest of Puerto Rico, this is followed by another period of celebration due to the octavas and octavitas.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>According to oral tradition, the Fiestas a la Santa Cruz have been celebrated since the municipality\'s foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino155_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino155-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Dorado also celebrates fiestas patronales to honor Antonio de Padua, which retain their religious origins but have included cultural activities such as trova contests, the coronation of a queen and La Alborada.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino155_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino155-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During these, the municipality also celebrates a Day of the Absent Dorade\xc3\xb1os, in which those abroad visit and join a celebration in their name.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino162_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino162-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other days are dedicated to exemplary mothers and adopted citizens (the official title of "Adoptive Son" is given during these).<sup id="cite_ref-Canino162_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino162-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> General recreation activities include horse races, carny attractions, sack races, climbing competitions and eating contests among others.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino168_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino168-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A variety of traditional food and sweets are also served.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino168_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino168-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Prior to Lent, a carnival is hosted, although the religious significance of the date has since been phased out beyond the interaction of the Vejigantes, La Muerte en Cueros and the Negritos (a Christian allegory with pagan elements depicting tormenting demons and death as the great equalizer in relation to sinners represented by the Negritos, taking away the enjoyment of the demons) and now host other cultural elements.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino175_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino175-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Catholic practices attributed to Lent are widely practiced, along local ones such as preserving palm branches from Palm Sunday as a practice to ward off ill wishes and bad luck.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino179_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino179-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Processions are celebrated during Easter week.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino181_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino181-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorado celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in June. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de San Antonio de Padua</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The festival has featured live performances by well-known artists such as <a href="/wiki/Raphy_Leavitt" title="Raphy Leavitt">Raphy Leavitt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismael_Miranda" title="Ismael Miranda">Ismael Miranda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Cap%C3%B3" title="Pedro Cap\xc3\xb3">Pedro Cap\xc3\xb3</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fiestas_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fiestas-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sign_for_Carnaval_del_Plata_in_Dorado,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sign_for_Carnaval_del_Plata_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Sign_for_Carnaval_del_Plata_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sign_for_Carnaval_del_Plata_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Sign_for_Carnaval_del_Plata_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sign_for_Carnaval_del_Plata_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Sign_for_Carnaval_del_Plata_in_Dorado%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2136" /></a><figcaption>Sign for <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Carnaval del Plata</i></span> in Dorado</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Dorado include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Three Kings\xe2\x80\x99 Day</a> Festival \xe2\x80\x93 January</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">Del Plata</a> Carnival \xe2\x80\x93 February</li>\n<li>Minin Kuilan Gold Cup \xe2\x80\x93 April</li>\n<li>Cocol\xc3\xada Crab Festival\xe2\x80\x93 August</li>\n<li>Town and Country Festival \xe2\x80\x93 September</li>\n<li>Discovery of Puerto Rico / Puerto Rican Culture Festival \xe2\x80\x93 November</li>\n<li>Christmas Festival \xe2\x80\x93 December</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Academics_and_arts">Academics and arts</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Academics and arts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>As a historically industrial town, the academic culture is mostly centered around writer Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada and poet Ferdinand R. Cestero is honored for employing the municipality as part of his pseudonym.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino145_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino145-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A Cultural Center supported by the ICP was founded in 1967, with the municipal Office of Cultural Affairs promoting these aspects begging during the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino182_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino182-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first local poet was Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 D\'Emulation award winner Camille Schwingrouber.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino146_128-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino146-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Former president of the Ateneo Puertorrique\xc3\xb1o Ferdinand R. Cestero wrote <i>Dorado, pueblito \xc3\xa1ureo y ensi\xc3\xb1ador...</i> to honor the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino147_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino147-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Son of former mayor Cruz Alegr\xc3\xada, Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada was born in Dorado on July 17, 1886, and went on to direct <i>Puerto Rico Illustrado</i> magazine and write several books.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino147_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino147-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He was also a painter, being instructed by Francisco Oller.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino148_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino148-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His son, Ricardo Alegr\xc3\xada, later became one of the most influential cultural figures in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino148_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino148-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Beginning in the 1970s, Pablo Maysonet began publishing several books.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino149_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino149-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Dorado Writers and Friends of Literature Circle was founded to promote literature, but ceased functioning by 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino149_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino149-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A local newspaper was first published in 1903, when El Hijo del Combate circulated.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino184_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino184-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Dorado Society of Archeological Investigations was founded in 1983 and is tasked with the archeological material at Museo Casa del Rey.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino183_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino183-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Until the 1930s, weekly bomba dances were held in Calle Norte and Calle Sur.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino156_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino156-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These were later preserved by the plena groups of Dorado.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino157_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino157-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other folkloric arts groups included Los Bat\xc3\xa1, Ballet Folkl\xc3\xb3rico Arawak, Ballet Folkl\xc3\xb3rico Aman\xc3\xa1 and other municipal and community groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino158_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino158-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the 1950s the municipal band and a Luteran band were created.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino151_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino151-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A school band combined the high school and middle school students during the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino151_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino151-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Mel\xc3\xa9ndez brothers, Manuel and Eleuterio, were Dorado\'s first professional musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino149_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino149-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Carmen Mel\xc3\xa9ndez, daughter of the second later taught piano in the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino149_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino149-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pedro, Andr\xc3\xa9s and Manuel, Jr., sons of Manuel, Sr. went on to play several instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino150_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino150-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pianist Lidia Morales, an alumnus of Ar\xc3\xadstiles Chavier, was also born in Dorado.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino150_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino150-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the 1960s, Germ\xc3\xa1n J\xc3\xadmenez composed a number of vals and danzas.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino150_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino150-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Marcos J. Alegr\xc3\xada was the municipality\'s first career painter.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino152_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino152-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the 1970s, the Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada school began teaching dramatic arts at the behest of Laura Iglesias.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino154_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino154-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the 1980s, a theatre named Teatro Juan Boria and  an arts school named Academia de Arte Dram\xc3\xa1tico Araman\xc3\xa1 were created, along a municipal theatre group.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino154_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino154-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other plastic artists that followed in his footsteps were Jaime Rivera, Marco A. Alegr\xc3\xada, Jes\xc3\xbas Cardona, Luis R. Nieves, Salvador Rivera and Basilio Cardona.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino153_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino153-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1919, Cine Juana de Arco was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino155_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino155-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Despite producing some athletes, sports were not widely promoted until the foundation of the intermunicipal Olimpiadas del Plata during the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino334_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino334-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The formal events include a marathon held in November.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino335_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino335-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paso_Fino" title="Paso Fino">Paso Fino</a>, an indigenous sport, has been among the most practiced, with the Kuilan family gaining prominence due to it.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino301_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino301-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Francisco Kuilan is a second generation rider and won competitions held locally and internationally in places like Paris, where he won a non-Paso Fino competition with a horse named Dulce Sue\xc3\xb1o in a tour sponsored by <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Ben%C3%ADtez_Rexach" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Ben\xc3\xadtez Rexach">F\xc3\xa9lix Ben\xc3\xadtez Rexach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino302_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino302-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He served as namesake for the Min\xc3\xadn Kuilan Cup, held by the municipality of Dorado since 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino303_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino303-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Local athletes include Manol\xc3\xadn Maldonado and Angel Maysonet, baseball players To\xc3\xb1o Cardona, Nol\xc3\xadn Valderrama, Arturito de Jes\xc3\xbas, Germ\xc3\xa1n Lanz\xc3\xb3, Pedro D\xc3\xadaz, Pito \xc3\x81lvarez, Peoe Carbia, Tom\xc3\xa1s Palmeras, Mampostial S\xc3\xa1nchez, Fabi\xc3\xa1n Cardona and Tal\xc3\xad Maldonado and chess player Cuc\xc3\xbc Alegr\xc3\xada, runners Juan Cruz and Millo Lorenzana, and boxers Tony Villa, Carmelo V\xc3\xa1zquez and Rafael Santana.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino335_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino335-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Dorado has its own Double A baseball team called <i>Los Guardianes</i> (The Guardians) and it\'s still one of the main places in the island to play golf or tennis. Within <a href="/wiki/Sports_entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports entertainment">sports entertainment</a>, professional wrestlers <a href="/wiki/Ray_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Ray Gonz\xc3\xa1lez">Ray Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Damian_Priest" title="Damian Priest">Damian Priest</a> were raised in the municipality.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Shrimp_boats_of_the_Dorado_Fishing_Cooperative_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="2003" /></a><figcaption>Shrimp boats acquired by the Dorado Fishing Cooperative in Puerto Rico in 1965</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In 2007, there were ten farms in Dorado, producing plantains, coffee, vegetables or melons, bananas, root crops or tubers, grains, grasses and other crops, poultry and eggs, cattle and calves, milk products, hogs and pigs, aquaculture, other livestock, and other livestock products. The top livestock produced in Dorado are cattle and calves, horses, hogs and pigs. The top crop items were lawn grass (sod), coffee, pigeon peas, cassava, and other vegetables.<sup id="cite_ref-2007_Census_of_Agriculture_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007_Census_of_Agriculture-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Business">Business</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Business"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Commerce\nTourism and pharmaceuticals.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Industry">Industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Dorado is the site of several industries dedicated to the manufacturing of clothing and medical equipment, among others. Companies like <a href="/wiki/Boston_Scientific" title="Boston Scientific">Boston Scientific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heraeus" title="Heraeus">Heraeus</a> are among some of the ones located in the city.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Housing_developments">Housing developments</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Housing developments"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In recent years, Dorado has been known for its development of upscale neighborhoods. Several known politicians and artists (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Romero_Barcel%C3%B3" title="Carlos Romero Barcel\xc3\xb3">Carlos Romero Barcel\xc3\xb3</a>) live or own properties in the city.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop{border-spacing:1px;border:1px solid class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />1899 (shown as 1900)<sup id="cite_ref-162" href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 1960\xe2\x80\x932000<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>Dorado\'s population has steadily increased during the past century. According to the 2000 census, the population consist of 34,017 with a population density of 1,479.0 people&#160;per square mile (571.0 people/km<sup>2</sup>) more than doubling the town\'s population of 17,388 in 1970. The 2020 census indicated the first decline (6%) since the U.S. census has been carried out on the island. According to the 2020 census the town has a population of 35,879.\n</p><p>As a whole, Puerto Rico is populated mainly by people from a <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">Criollo</a> (born on the island of Spanish descent) or European descent, with small groups of <a href="/wiki/Afro%E2%80%93Puerto_Ricans" title="Afro\xe2\x80\x93Puerto Ricans">African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_Americans" title="Asian Americans">Asian</a> descent. Statistics taken from the 2000 census shows that 74.1% of Dorade\xc3\xb1os identify with Spanish or <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a> origin, 12.2% identify as <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black</a>, and 0.5% as <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a>.\n</p><p>As of 2000, speakers of English as a first language accounted for 16.89% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="3">Race \xe2\x80\x93 Dorado, Puerto Rico \xe2\x80\x93 2000 Census<sup races</b></td>\n<td>1,213</td>\n<td>3.6%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religious_affiliation">Religious affiliation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Religious affiliation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Due to the influence of Spanish culture, a majority of Dorado\'s population still practices Catholicism. There are two religious patrons, the Virgen del Rosario and Antonio Abad.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino333_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino333-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Esteban Mariani was placed in charge of the Dorado Parish on June 29, 1848.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino323_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino323-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since then, several priests served the function until Salvador Carratala was charged in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino323_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino323-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Afterwards, the Dominican Fathers took over in 1927 and held the office until Salvador Pujolas\' one-year stint in 1930.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino324_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino324-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The following year, the Augustinian Fathers took over until handling it to the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_of_the_Mission" title="Congregation of the Mission">Congregation of the Mission</a> in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino324_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino324-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The following year, Jos\xc3\xa9 Delgado was tasked with the parish until the Holy Spirit Fathers took over in 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino324_173-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino324-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The Getseman\xc3\xad Lutheran Church was founded on July 25, 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino327_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino327-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Initially ran by foreign ministers, until Demetrio Texidor consecrated a temple in August 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino327_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino327-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On December 30, 1945, Carlos Torres became the first officially installed reverend serving the office for 5 years, after years of the office being distributed between locals and foreigners.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino328_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino328-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the following years, the entity continued its expansion plans under Miguel Sevilla.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino328_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino328-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1954, Victor Astacio took over and under him the Church hosted its first synod of the Caribbean event.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino328_175-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino328-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1961, Gilberto Falc\xc3\xb3n took over and began a project to construct a new temple with the old one hosting its last service on July 19, 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino329_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino329-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Rafael Malpica Padilla, a Dorade\xc3\xb1o, also served as reverend.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino329_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino329-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the 1950s, the Lutheran Church created a club for performing arts, where they enacted plays that were mostly centered around nativity.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino154_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino154-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1920s, Leonor Mart\xc3\xadnez of Centro Espiritista Caridad bajo Gloria organized several dramatic works to gather funds for the spiritist organization.<sup id="cite_ref-Canino154_154-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canino154-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>All municipalities in Puerto Rico are administered by a mayor, elected every four years. The current mayor of Dorado is <a href="/wiki/Carlos_L%C3%B3pez_Rivera" title="Carlos L\xc3\xb3pez Rivera">Carlos L\xc3\xb3pez Rivera</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a> (PPD). He was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_1988" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 1988">1988 general elections</a>.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district III">Puerto Rico Senatorial district III</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_P%C3%A9rez_Rosa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 P\xc3\xa9rez Rosa">Jos\xc3\xa9 "Joito" P\xc3\xa9rez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angel_Mart%C3%ADnez_Santiago" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel Mart\xc3\xadnez Santiago">Angel Mart\xc3\xadnez</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The official flag of the Municipality of Dorado is made up of three stripes of equal width and the symbols from the coat of arms are within the brown stripe, in a sideways position. A first stripe of gold is followed by a stripe of brown which is followed by a final stripe of gold. The gold or golden stripes symbolize the town\'s name, Dorado; and the brown stripe represents the patron Saint of Dorado, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_of_Padua" title="Anthony of Padua">Saint Anthony of Padua</a>. A brown, equal-sided triangle is placed with its base at the hoist and leads to the second stripe, inside of which are the disks in the shape of a T and with the lily flowers represented with the <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">Fleur-de-lis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_of_Puerto_Rico_2007_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_of_Puerto_Rico_2007-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Dorado coat of arms was officially adopted on March 27, 1978. Its colors are gold, silver and brown. The three towers at the top are enameled in gold with brown background for windows. The triple tower represents that Dorado is a town, and a municipality.\n</p><p>Below the mural crown, are five disks which form a letter "T", called <a href="/wiki/Tau" title="Tau">Tau</a>. This represents <a href="/wiki/Anthony_of_Padua" title="Anthony of Padua">Saint Anthony of Padua</a>, who is associated with the lily flower. Saint Anthony of Padua is depicted with a lily, heraldically with the <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">Fleur-de-lis</a>. They have a brown background and the lily flowers are silver because they represent the majestic <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_(Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado de la Plata (Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado La Plata</a> ("plata" is Spanish for silver), which borders the town of Dorado to the east.\n</p><p>The golden background with the brown disks are like speaking souls (Spanish: <i lang="es">almasparlantes</i>). The shield directly represents the name of the town "Dorado" which means "gold" in Spanish and the brown relates to the Patron Saint Anthony of Padua, whose <a href="/wiki/Biblical_clothing" title="Biblical clothing">habit</a> is brown.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_of_Puerto_Rico_2007_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_of_Puerto_Rico_2007-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Dorado has several public and private schools distributed through several regions. Including <a href="/wiki/TASIS" class="mw-redirect" title="TASIS">TASIS</a>, Dorado Academy, New Testament Christian Academy of Dorado, and Public education is handled by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Education" title="Puerto Rico Department of Education">Puerto Rico Department of Education</a>.\n</p><p>Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada is the public High School, located in the town center. Ricardo Arroyo Laracuente is the Middle School 7th through 9th Grade. In the town next to the town square is the elementary School named Jacinto L\xc3\xb3pez Mart\xc3\xadnez.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Schools_and_academies">Schools and academies</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Schools and academies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>Dorado Academy</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/TASIS_Dorado" class="mw-redirect" title="TASIS Dorado">TASIS Dorado</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_S._Alegr%C3%ADa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada">Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada</a> High School</li>\n<li>Pedro L\xc3\xb3pez Canino Elementary and Middle School</li>\n<li>Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Elementary School</li>\n<li>Ricardo Arroyo Middle School</li>\n<li>Marcelino Canino Canino \xe2\x80\x93 Middle School</li>\n<li>Jacinto L\xc3\xb3pez Mart\xc3\xadnez \xe2\x80\x93 Elementary school and first school building to be founded in Dorado. It is over a hundred years old and still in use and one of the biggest schools.</li>\n<li>Luisa Valderrama Mart\xc3\xadnez \xe2\x80\x93 Elementary school</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jsdcl.org/">The Jane Stern Dorado Community Library</a>, founded in 1974, is Puerto Rico\'s first public bilingual library. Recipient of a 2008 <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_for_Museum_and_Library_Service" title="National Medal for Museum and Library Service">National Medal for Museum and Library Service</a>.</li>\n<li>Crist\xc3\xb3bal Santana Melecio Elementary School</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Health_care">Health care</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Health care"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Dorado\'s main health facility is a Center for Diagnostic and Treatment located at Road 698. The facility is able to handle emergency cases, but severe cases are transferred to bigger hospitals in nearby towns such as <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a> or <a href="/wiki/Manat%C3%AD,_Puerto_Rico" title="Manat\xc3\xad, Puerto Rico">Manat\xc3\xad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_22" title="Puerto Rico Highway 22">Puerto Rico Highway 22</a> provides access to Dorado from the far away city of <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>, or from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>. Road 165 also provides access from <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a> bordering the shore to the Atlantic Ocean. It takes approximately 30 minutes to reach the town from San Juan.\n</p><p>Like most other towns in the island, it has a public transportation system consisting of public cars. Taxis are also available around the town. There\'s also a public <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trolley</a> system around town and a shuttle service for handicapped people.\n</p><p>There are 19 bridges in Dorado.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dorado_Airport" title="Dorado Airport">Dorado Airport</a> was a commercial airport that served the city with flights to San Juan and to the United States, but it has since been closed.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorado,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notable residents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_S._Alegr%C3%ADa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada">Jos\xc3\xa9 S. Alegr\xc3\xada</a>, poet, writer, lawyer and politician.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Juan_Boria" title="Juan Boria">Juan Boria</a>, poet</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Onix_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="Onix Concepci\xc3\xb3n">Onix Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a>, Major League Baseball shortstop</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Damian_Priest" title="Damian Priest">Damian Priest</a>, professional wrestler and former WWE World Champion</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
